# Appendix for today's intraday post

> Rangebounding, spot decay, liquidity, insider speculation

**Date:** 2025-01-29T22:11:46.429Z
**Source:** https://stochvoltrader.substack.com/p/appendix-for-todays-intraday-post

---

Market analysisAppendix for today's intraday postRangebounding, spot decay, liquidity, insider speculationMar 13, 20254144ShareProloge:Todayâ€™s intraday post - algo predicts oscillating regime, eased negativ driftGeopolitical context - borning US-Russia-ME alliance, its conditions, shift in the geopolitical landscapeRecent weekly post - geopolitics interaction with the market In my todayâ€™s premarket post, there were four main statements:1) Local gamma is low, even negative, and the theoretically derived mechanical flows favor for further gamma decay as time passes2) Realized volatility is bid, implied vol is relatively underperformed during the spot decay, and so liquidity is low3) We are just right at the JHEQX collar current long put strike, in a net positive speed environment into EOM, thus MMs are long vanna4) Despite the geopolitical uncertainities, heavy bearishness, gov shutdown concerns, and growth scare, we see fixed strike skew for both SPX and VIX kinda stagnant and even shorter into the quarterly OpEx (and lower than it was on this Monday), absolutely crushed into EOM, and below its Monday lvl into this Friday expo, along with positive SPX/LTY correlation (good news are good news, bad news are bad news) Nowâ€¦ this is a significant discrepancy hereâ€¦ Subscribe The whole narrative behind the spot decay was to protect the market from a violent volatility squeeze and to gradually lower the market under relatively low volatility conditions. Thatâ€™s why I called it an "oscillation with negative drift." Volatility underperformed, and the grind up of the vol complex was slow enough to keep the spot/vol beta sticky. With this approach, insiders were able, on one hand, to buy out opposing positions from certain sectors like tech and commodities; on the other hand, they managed to drive prices lower in the tech sector to make it more attractive to Middle Eastern investors around Q3; and thirdly, through the negative wealth effect, they will force the Fed into implementing QE, while not letting bears to fully capitalize on the bear-side.  Iâ€™ve written extensively about this since the February OpEx, and by now you understand it. However, this level is not yet enough to sufficiently slow down growth. I mention this because itâ€™s important to understand that last yearâ€™s rally was entirely one long, protracted short squeeze through the derivatives marketâ€”I posted a lot about that last year. A deeper level is needed, and this fake liquidityâ€”upon which last yearâ€™s and this yearâ€™s all-time highs were builtâ€”must be washed out, because it is unstable. In the upcoming future geopolitical structure and alliance systems, the US needs stable growth, not one based on manias and bubbles.They have to solve it this year. (This is why I called to hit â€˜24 April lows) The problem is that by the time the spot reached the JPM long put strike and fell to 5532 (from which we went long gaining 100+ points in recent days), liquidity simply dried up because everyone ended up on the same side of the trade. And without liquidity, the market canâ€™t function as it should. The VIX got stuck at a high 26â€“27 level while the market was moving downward. Already on Tuesday, I saw signs of falling volatility in my stochvol models; also the HMM predicted a regime shift, and then this trend became visibly apparent both in the SPX and in the VIX vol smirk, as I mentioned premarket.  Additionally, L/S performance shows improvement in semis and AI, and the synthetic negative gamma supply is also decreasing, with the VIX significantly underperforming since Mondayâ€” as its drop was 2 vol points larger than what the SPX moves would have implied. However, we are in a situation of significant negative gamma, and if the vol of vol rises again and a vol crush occurs, then in the Mag7-8â€”which has a historically elevated put skewâ€”there is squeeze risk. This, in turn, would lead to a spot up/vol up scenario in the indexâ€¦ again.What can be done? Well, if Citadel, BlackRock, JPM, Goldman, and the other â€˜highly respectedâ€™ leaders get together to resolve this situation, they could have their quant teams switch their algorithms to mean reversion trading after buying in at a smaller size at Tuesdayâ€™s 5528 level, thereby providing the market with some liquidity. This wouldnâ€™t create upside momentum, but it would compress the intraday range, filling the market with liquidity, which naturally suppresses volatility. At the same time, the market is simply oscillating (as my model predicted after yesterdayâ€™s close, posted today premarket), and it can just as easily catch both bears and bulls off guard. Range-bound trading is Wall Streetâ€™s favorite toyâ€”we saw it back in 2022, and itâ€™s the same game now.Now here comes the twist! The JPM collar position is a very large one, with the short call strike at 6165 and a long put debit spread at 5565/4700 (with market makers taking the opposite side). Essentially, until the expiry at the end of March, this position fundamentally determines the vanna and speed exposure for the mechanical flows. As long as the market oscillates above the long put strike and volatility comes down, the market makersâ€™ long vanna effect produces a weak supportive flow for the market. However, letâ€™s not forget that the JPM long put strike represents a significant short gamma for the market makers. At that point, both the speed profile and the vanna profile reverse.Pay close attention: If the market falls from above toward the 5565 market maker short gamma strike, then due to the long vanna effect, market makers will have shorter vega, which naturally increases volatility.But below the strike, this reverses: if the market continues to fall toward the market makersâ€™ 4700 long gamma strike, then they will have longer vega due to the short vanna, which naturally decreases volatility. Now, as long as volatility remains sticky at elevated levels above the short gamma strike, the vanna effect is supportive below the collar strike, since high volatility results in a shorter delta in a negative speed negative vanna environment. Why? Because vanna is nearly zero where gamma is at its lowest. Therefore, when the spot approaches the short gamma strike from above, as volatility rises and dealers acquire longer delta positions, the vanna effect weakens, eventually becomes zero, and then reverses below the strike. However, all positions can be bridged on a weekly or even intraday basis. By this, I mean that if volatility does not rise but rather falls around the short gamma strike, then the spot can break through the strike and close below itâ€”and furthermore, from that point on, decreasing volatility, combined with the negative vanna effect, will push the spot lower and lower, along with the positive charm flow, toward the other end of the speed profile at the 4700 strike. But according to the code, the braking effect can already be felt around 5114.24. At those levels, the algorithms generate significant liquidity, culminating in a slow grind of spot down/vol down. Note, that my model isnâ€™t saying that the negative drift has suddenly become zero, but rather that itâ€™s now very small (written today). In other words, the downward trend is still there, but weâ€™re seeing strong oscillations that push volatility down, gradually guiding momentum across the JPM long put strike.(Thatâ€™s why many people mistakenly believe that the JPM short gamma strike has any pinning effectâ€”but this is a misconception.) Therefore, my current tactic is a short vol trade, as I written premarket, without any directional take. We need to watch where we stand relative to the collar strike. With this, the insiders achieve three things: 1) they fill the market with liquidity while 2) driving the spot down to a deep level that triggers QE and encourages buying by Russian and Middle Eastern investors, and 3) when they close the collar at the end of March, and it is ITM, the buyback flow induces supportive flow without an elevated spot/vol beta. This scenario is important to consider, which is why I continuously emphasize that we proceed day by day here and closely monitor the volatility cycles. In an environment like this, do not get married to either side. Thatâ€™s a golden rule! Itâ€™s all about the volatility trade as I keep sayingâ€¦Subscribe to Stochastic Volatility Trader - Quant InsightsBy AlmaMarket analysis | Trading strategies | Educational content | No financial adviseSubscribeBy subscribing, you agree Substack's Terms of Use, and acknowledge its Information Collection Notice and Privacy Policy.41 Likesâˆ™4 Restacks4144SharePreviousNext

April's performance reviewFor all Subscribers...May 14, 2025318ShareDear Subscribers,Recently I received some criticism about the macro content from last April. I admit this topic is very complex and hard to understand, but letâ€™s not forget: the primary purpose of this Substack is to teach tape analysis, and macro processes are a key part of that game.Stochastic Volatility - Options market insights is a reader-supported publication. To receive new posts and support my work, consider becoming a free or paid subscriber.SubscribeYou have to understand that â€œin the short run, the market is a voting machine; in the long run, it is a weighing machine,â€ as Benjamin Graham taught usâ€”and Aprilâ€™s weakness was the weighing machine, not the voting one. Once that â€˜weighing machineâ€™ has been turned on, it has restructured the market and set it on a new path. To monitor and interpret news, data, and policy shifts in the future, you need to understand the story behind the curtain that volatility cycles are telling. Not to mention that in such a high-volatility environmentâ€”when weâ€™re literally in the tails, as we saw over the past few weeksâ€”usual mechanical and structural flows simply donâ€™t work. Instead, I explained the dynamics that did matter.The events will show up on the tape one way or another, but to understand why the market reacts in a certain, seemingly irrational way, youâ€™ve got to grasp the real meaning behind those events. If you remember Trumpâ€™s speeches back in February and Marchâ€”and the marketâ€™s unpredictable swingsâ€”you know exactly what I mean. Iâ€™ve basically decoded all of that for you, and my goal was to walk you through how I arrived at those conclusions.The market is ultimately about valuing things at its core. If you grasp this, youâ€™ll see that volatility cycles always need to have a narrativeâ€”otherwise theyâ€™re neither manageable nor sustainable. Thatâ€™s why the story matters.(And Iâ€™m glad I didnâ€™t launch the Substack during a dull bull-market rally, but in a year when the global economic landscape is literally being repolarized.)A good analyst needs to be able to switch between approaches and pinpoint the key driver behind volatility cycles. I recognized in time that it was the macro and geo environment and front-ran the events effectively. Now that the weighing machine has reset the market regimeâ€”forcing it onto a new pathâ€”and the volatility market has adapted accordingly, we can return to microstructures, because the story is finally unfolding and the context is taking shape. This is how cycles work. One day youâ€™ll get it.This may seem strange way of approach, but it produced results. And please allow me to analyze things the way I think they should be analyzed!  Since many people got lost in the information, I made a quick review of Aprilâ€™s performance in terms of momentum. I also posted this on Twitterâ€”here you can see it:â€œWas it perfect? -Not at all. But at least, it was realâ€ Somebody also sent me a PDF. He scanned all my posts since March, checked for consistencies and inconsistencies, and compared my posts to the actual realized events. He/they estimated my April hit rate around 91%, and my trade signals hit rate around 80-82%â€¦ in a historically high vol environmentâ€¦Here you can read it. I think it is a good summary and review. # Earning season, Micro and Macro flows, Carry trade & Geopolitic landscape | Quant Insights - January 2026

> [FREE]

**Date:** 2025-01-29T22:11:46.429Z

Free Insights | Market ReportsEarning season, Micro and Macro flows, Carry trade & Geopolitic landscape | Quant Insights - January 2026[FREE]Jan 23, 20263023ShareGeo context including â€œBoard of Peaceâ€: Board of Peace, Greenland, Hidden Left-tail and Kurtosis | Geopolitical Developments [FREE]AlmaÂ·Jan 20Read full storyAI/tech boom, overvaluation, bubble-burst triggers, geopolitical landscape, description of the coming crisis: The challenges of 2026AlmaÂ·Jan 5Read full storySubscribeBank of Japan & USDJPYIâ€™ve already discussed the significance of the BoJ rate decision in my weekly post. This is what I wrote:â€œFor BoJ, most coverage points to a hold at 0.75% (after the December hike to 0.75%). As said in the yearly post, I expect a pause in rate hikes during the first half of the year. Which, if markets are leaning that way too, reduces the chance of a rates shockâ€¦ but it heightens the sensitivity to any sign the BoJ is drifting away from that patience. So now, carry conditions can persist.However, if communication pushes investors to price earlier tightening, US momentum stock - selling can be expected (Japanese investors have accumulated dollars and bought US equities and bonds, often unhedged, in part because the yen depreciated for years and Japanese policy rates were extremely low).It depends on how much the gov worries of the near-term import inflation.â€Japanâ€™s government bond market saw a sharp sell-off: yields pushed above multi-decade highs, while the yen weakened to multi-month lows.  The driver is rising fiscal uncertaintyâ€”and, with it, a higher risk premium. This is reminiscent of the UK in 2022, when a fiscal-credibility shock sent gilt yields soaring and impaired financial stability, prompting the Bank of England to launch a temporary, targeted longâ€‘gilt purchase programme to restore â€œorderly market conditionsâ€.Fitch has argued that the deficits are manageable, but it also highlighted that Japanâ€™s debt ratio remains the highest among advanced economiesâ€”on the order of >230% of GDP.In this context, the Ministry of Financeâ€™s efforts to support the yen may prove insufficient. As an IMF publication notes:So if the market starts to price in fiscal dominance (i.e., monetary policy being forced to safeguard the governmentâ€™s financing capacity), then 1) part of the bond-market premium can migrate into FX, and 2) the yen becomes the balance-sheet â€œcollateralâ€ through which the system reprices. The rise in yields therefore is no longer a â€œrewardâ€ (carry), but a â€œpenaltyâ€ (risk premium).But then how can the yen be holding up against the USD?Because the USâ€“EU diplomatic dispute has given de-dollarization fresh momentum, and the yen is weakening primarily against the euro instead:This is crucial from a carry-trade perspective, because Japan effectively has only two choices: 1) accept higher interest rates and risk a debt crisis, or 2) cap yieldsâ€”in which case the yen depreciates. However, the â€œsell Americaâ€ momentum may, in the short run, mask yen weakness versus the dollar, yet it embeds asymmetric tail risk, as the yen could start trading like a â€œfiscal stress / riskâ€‘offâ€ currency. The carry trade has therefore deteriorated in quality: for the same tail risk, there is less potential upside in USD/JPY if the USD is falling on its own.Looking at inflation passâ€‘through and potential policy responses, my view remains that yen weakness may still be with us through the first half of 2026. Later, however, the yen could strengthen back toward ~140 against the dollarâ€”especially if the USâ€“EU diplomatic dispute is resolved. The main reason is the rise in imported inflation driven by the weak yen, which the central bank will ultimately have to manage.   But the most important reason is the weakness of the dollar, ultimately leading to USDâ€‘carry deleveraging.SPX & NDXThe geopolitical realignmentâ€”and with it, de-dollarizationâ€”continues.Since 1 January, the SPX is up 0.8% in USD terms, but it is down 0.11% in EUR terms and down 9.75% when measured in gold.The same pattern holds for the NDX: it is up 1.24% in USD terms, but only up 0.26% in EUR terms, and it is down 9.72% when measured in gold.Retail trading volumes in January 2026 are running ~40% above the average January level over 2020â€“2025, in both cash equities and options. This flow is on the supportive side and, in the short run, shows up as persistent negative speed exposure on the marketâ€‘maker side. (Most of the activity is concentrated in stocks linked to rare earths, the drone industry, nuclear energy, and cryptoâ€‘related themes.) This implies that traders are typically short OTM puts and long OTM callsâ€”creating synthetic leverage via dealer hedging flows on the bid, while reflexively suppressing downside volatility. That, in turn, triggers local hedge unwinds and vol compression, and therefore additional volâ€‘control buyback flows and positive rebalancing flows. The effect is likely to growâ€”especially given that Nasdaq has recently approved Monday and Wednesday singleâ€‘stock option expirations (in the mould of 0DTE options), which should further lift retail volumes by improving flexibility. It is therefore unsurprising that the most heavily shorted stocks have outperformed in recent weeks. Another important aspect is that volâ€‘ofâ€‘vol is also being soldâ€”both synthetically and directlyâ€”via deep OTM put selling, VIX call selling, institutional buyback programmes (Citadel, BlackRock), and outflows from moneyâ€‘market funds. This applies both to the bond market (â€œBessent putâ€) and to the equity market.This is reinforced by moneyâ€‘market funds (MMFs), whichâ€”as I flagged over the course of last yearâ€”have begun to shrink their asset base: Since the start of the year, roughly a 1.35% outflow (in dollar terms) has occurred, which is the largest timeâ€‘adjusted outflow since April 2025. This suggests that parked cash has started to rotate back into riskier assets in early 2026. The liquid reserves accumulated in MMFs therefore represent potential buying firepower for equity and bond markets over the coming weeks.The net effect is that the kurtosis of the expected return distribution is being compressed: the left tail is still present, but its magnitude has been materially reduced.In other words, due to intervention by large market participants, the market can only experience managed, temporary drawdowns; they are not allowing it to collapse. In the short run, an illusion of stability is being maintained; over the longer run, however, risks are accumulating. More on that later. For now, the objective is to keep frontâ€‘end volatility and volâ€‘ofâ€‘vol in check, because both the market and the broader geopolitical backdrop are on the cusp of a regime shift. The market is being protected at all costs from a larger crash that would deteriorate economic statistics and sentiment.Yearâ€‘toâ€‘date, RTY has outperformed NDX by roughly 7.3%â€”meaning that on every day of 2026 so far, small caps have outperformed megaâ€‘cap technology: This behaviour is also evident in the broader SPX. Since 29 October, a modest rotation out of technology has been visible:There has also been significant rotation within the top 100 blueâ€‘chip names since 29 October: However, the rotation has primarily been led by tech: At the same time, market breadth has genuinely been improving since 29 October:In other words, it is no longer just a handful of megaâ€‘caps pulling the indices higher; an increasing number of sectors are contributing to todayâ€™s index level. I warned about this trend last year, and this broadening helps damp volatilityâ€”and the effect is only strengthening:This rotation is, on the one hand, a consolidation phase for tech, and on the other hand, an early signal of pressure coming from the European Union and China. With volatility being capped, the bullâ€“bear spread is running at roughly three times its longâ€‘run average. This reflects strong optimism, and abundant retail liquidity can provide nearâ€‘term supportâ€”especially during minor pullbacks. At the same time, as equity participation broadens, attention shifts toward sector rotation and fundamentals rather than purely index moves, whichâ€”as I notedâ€”are being managed in order to keep the distribution under control against external shocks.Yields curvesFor most of 2025, the US yield curve was extremely flat and inverted; in early 2026 it appears to have reached a technical â€œsupportâ€ level. Over recent weeks, asset managers have begun buying longerâ€‘dated bonds and selling shorterâ€‘dated paperâ€”effectively putting on curve steepeners.At the same time, CTA strategies in rates remain positioned short: globally they are net sellers of bond futures, especially in the long end, while partially hedging via some buying in the front end. This suggests that systematic models are still leaning toward higher yieldsâ€”consistent with a reflation narrative. The current USâ€“EU standoff adds fuel to that dynamic, although the pressure is likely to be concentrated more in the technology sector. As I also wrote last December, I continue to view deep OTM put hedges in the US rates market as a desirable position.Since New Yearâ€™s the 2sâ€“5s spread has widened by 12.27%:The 2sâ€“10s yield spread has widened by 11.67%: The 2sâ€“30s spread has widened by 12.25%:In all three cases, current levels are sitting between their 10â€‘year and 30â€‘year moving averages.Overall, a normalization process is starting to take shapeâ€”at least, that is the intended path. The market remains sensitive to political and inflation headlines, but overall liquidity has not deteriorated materially. The continuous presence of large institutional liquidity providers (e.g., Citadel Securities) provides a buffer effect: they have continued to supply bid/offer liquidity even through volatile episodes. Pricing in rates derivatives (e.g., interest rate swaps, FRAs) indicates that investors are pricing roughly one Fed rate cut in 2026, which is expected to stabilize the long end of the curve. There have also been strong inflows into global bond funds at the start of the year. Approximately ~$16.8 billion has gone into bond ETFs globally, with notable allocations into intermediateâ€‘maturity government bond ETFs (roughly a 2â€“3 standardâ€‘deviation inflow versus typical levels) and into municipal bond funds. A meaningful rotation is underway: money is flowing out of highâ€‘yield credit (â€“1.5 standard deviations), while flowing into investmentâ€‘grade bonds (+1.2 standard deviations). This points to a more cautious, qualityâ€‘tilted investor posture. CFTC data likewise show leveraged funds net short US long bonds, while having established some net long exposure on the short end.Meanwhile, asset managersâ€™ nearâ€‘record VIX short positioning suggests they are also looking for equity volatility to decline alongside bonds. Beyond indicating improved risk appetite, this implies an expectation of further upside in the near termâ€”driven by fiscal and monetary stimulusâ€”while inflation is not being treated as an immediate risk. That last point is critical.Gold and other metalsGold is up 85.85% since January 2025.The rally has been driven by three key forces: 1) An increasingly uncertain geopolitical backdrop and regime transition (e.g., concerns around Fed independence; USâ€“Iran tensions; USâ€“EU friction; USâ€“China conflict; etc.); 2) Monetary-policy expectations, as anticipated US rate cuts reduce the opportunity cost of holding gold, and 3) central-bank demand and ETF inflows: central banks purchased a record amount of gold in 2025 (e.g., China has been accumulating gold reserves for 14 consecutive months), while physically backed gold ETFs saw $89bn of net inflows over the yearâ€”also a historical high. In addition, the worldâ€™s largest gold ETF, SPDR Gold Trust, increased its holdings to 1,073 tonnes by endâ€‘2025, the highest level in three years.Back in the summer-autumn of last year, I wrote that in my view gold would move above $5,000â€“$5,200 by this yearâ€‘endâ€”which is not an encouraging signal for the macro environment.No fear of recessionHere I want to draw attention to an important process. Letâ€™s look at gold relative to copper. In the chart below, you can see the copperâ€‘toâ€‘gold ratio versus US 10â€‘year Treasury yields (cyan) since January 2025:First, as context: among industrial metals, copper and related metals strengthened in early 2026, in parallel with analysts upgrading global growth expectations. Over the past few weeks, CTAs have also built long positions in both copper and gold (copper longs are around the 80th percentile). Meanwhile, $4.5bn flowed into commodity ETFs in a single week. Within that, roughly $3.7bn went into preciousâ€‘metals ETFs (primarily gold, e.g., GLD), $0.5bn into energyâ€‘commodity ETFs (an unusually strong inflowâ€”more than 3 standard deviations), and meaningful inflows also hit industrialâ€‘metals ETFs (roughly a 4.9â€‘sigma anomaly).This matters because copper is a faithful proxy for global demand in the real economyâ€”it is a foundational â€œcivilization metal.â€ Across many analyses, copper prices (especially YoY changes) tend to coâ€‘move with manufacturing activity (e.g., ISM Manufacturing PMI). Gold, by contrast, is a safe havenâ€”a monetary hedge. It typically performs well when risk aversion rises and/or when the appeal of yieldâ€‘bearing alternatives declines. Importantly, this downtrend in the ratio did not begin recently; it began in 2021: Since October 2021, the ratio has fallen 55.02%â€”meaning gold has significantly outperformed copperâ€”while 10â€‘year yields are up by 158.68%, i.e., the discount rate / financing hurdle has moved dramatically higher.Over this period, the rise in yields was driven primarily by an increase in the term premium, fueled by quantitative tightening, heavier Treasury issuance, and elevated uncertaintyâ€”while the growth/demand side was deteriorating. That is a classic stagflationary signal.However, I would add that throughout this periodâ€”until early 2025â€”the SPX/yields correlation showed a net negative tendency:In practice, that meant the market was primarily labeling inflation as the key risk, rather than slowing growth. During the 2022 bear market, sentiment tilted somewhat toward the view that â€œtoo much tighteningâ€ could push the economy into recession, but by 2023 the market once again consistently treated inflation as the dominant risk. From Q3 2024, the assessment began shifting again toward the view that slowing growth was becoming a larger risk than inflation. Even so, over the past five years the correlation has been net negative overallâ€”suggesting the longâ€‘run risk remains inflation, while the market still views a slowdown as manageable. That is a reasonable stance: with rates still relatively high, markets can expect additional monetary support if neededâ€”but conditionally, that support should not undermine the softâ€‘landing narrative.This is internally consistent. If long yields are not being driven by a â€œgrowth scare,â€ but instead by term premium and supply factors, then the classic riskâ€‘off hedge function is impaired. Moreover, a persistently negative SPX/yield correlation can itself contribute to a higher term premium.Gold, meanwhile, is being driven primarily by geopolitics, rather than functioning purely as an inflation hedge. Centralâ€‘bank gold demand in 2024 accounted for more than 20% of global demand, and after 2022 geopolitical factors gained prominence; the traditional realâ€‘yield correlation has also broken down.Copper has not collapsed either: while the classic China fixedâ€‘asset investment impulse has slowed, electrification (EVs, grids, renewables, data centers / AI) has introduced a new secular demand engine. Put simply, gold continues to outperform copper.That points to a powerful supplyâ€‘side and fragmentation shock.Tariffs, sanctions, logistical rerouting, and rising compliance costs slow and raise the cost of moving inputs. Supply chains are being reâ€‘engineered (friendâ€‘shoring, as I wrote about last year), and the required transport/inventory buffers are increasing. In effect, geopolitics is importing supplyâ€‘chain inflation into the global system: trade frictions and delays impair global throughput and can ultimately lead to developments (capex deferrals, tighter financing conditions, higher uncertainty) that damage global industrial demand.Over the same period, the copperâ€‘toâ€‘SPX ratio fell by roughly 24%. Taken together, these signals clearly suggest growing tension between financial asset prices and the physical cycle. In my view, equity cash flows have been â€œpainted prettierâ€ than underlying physical demand: organic growth is minimal, and financial results have been inflated through M&A accounting, buybacks, and accrual mechanicsâ€”artificially reducing the apparent degree of overvaluation, in a creditâ€‘saturated system that Wall Street is happy to believe.In the near term, this can still be managed via soâ€‘called â€œsynthetic QEâ€ (like MBS demand by the GSEs, tariffâ€‘related stimulus checks, OBBBA fiscal stimulus, which could lift GDP growth by roughly 1%), tax rebates, caps on creditâ€‘card interest rates, prescriptionâ€‘drug price reforms, and Bessentâ€™s longâ€‘term yield managementâ€”and later via monetary easing under a new Fed chair. But this embeds longâ€‘run inflation risk and a creditâ€‘crisis risk into the systemâ€”on a much broader scale than twenty years ago.On the nature and drivers of the approaching crisis (including the AI/tech bubble, inflation dynamics, geopolitics, future regulation, and demographic aspects), I wrote in detail in the post below: The challenges of 2026AlmaÂ·Jan 5Read full storyCTAs, Vol Control, Risk Parity Funds, InvestorsVolatility suppression embeds additional asymmetric risk. A volatilitÃ¡s szupressziÃ³jÃ¡ra vÃ¡laszul a CTA modellek 2026 elejÃ©n Ã¶sszessÃ©gÃ©ben long pozÃ­ciÃ³ban vannak a rÃ©szvÃ©nyekben globÃ¡lis szinten, ugyanakkor a piaci esÃ©sre valÃ³ Ã©rzÃ©kenysÃ©gÃ¼k nÅ‘tt.In response to volatility suppression, CTA models are, on balance, long equities globally in early 2026, but their sensitivity to a downside move has increased. The major US equity indices are only about 1â€“2% away from the level at which CTAs, under their short-term trading rules, would begin to turn into net sellers. For now, they were still net buyers in energy last week (on the back of higher oil prices) and sellers in bonds. It is important to highlight the asymmetric risk embedded in CTA positioning. According to their model projections, if indices move sideways for a week, they would exert only modest selling pressure, and they would be incremental buyers (about 0.27x times smaller trade) if markets rise. By contrast, a one-week move lower could generate roughly 6.65x time bigger size of selling (than initially). Over longer horizons the asymmetry becomes even more pronounced. On a one-month horizon, a sideways market could imply around 2.7x bigger size of selling (than initially), while a 5% decline could trigger approximately 13.20x size more of potential selling, versus only about 0.07x smaller size of buying in a similarly sized rally. In other words, CTA models add only limited upside demand, but they de-risk much more aggressively on the downside.Volatility-control funds (which adjust portfolio weights as a function of realised volatility) are currently running extremely high equity exposure, around 95â€“98%. With realised volatility as low as it is, these models are at or near maximum equity weights. As a result, there is limited capacity for further incremental equity buying from this cohort, but if volatility spikes they will automatically become sellers as well, and in an asymmetric way.Risk-parity funds are similarly near 75â€“80% exposure, which is historically very overweight, while having slightly reduced commodity exposure. This indicates that multi-asset systematic strategies are positioned optimistically, taking advantage of the quieter tape, but in a volatility shock many could be forced to sell simultaneously.Investor sentiment has not improved. Funds are diversifying, scaling down exposure to US assets, and participating primarily via short-term, speculative momentum strategies. The Cboe COR3M Index is at a two-year low, reflecting elevated rotation. Index options have become relatively expensive versus single-stock options, as demand for hedges has increased across the 1â€“5 year horizon.Corporate buyback windowAs we approach the end of January 2026, an important technical development is the reopening of corporate share-repurchase windows. Due to earnings season, many companies have been in blackout since mid-December and were unable to repurchase shares. That buyback quiet period expires in late January/early February, so corporate repurchases should re-accelerate from February, providing an additional demand backstop and further compressing the kurtosis of the return distribution.Historically, February has been negative in 48.38% of observations. Strong January inflows often lose momentum, and February brings a correction before the market regains strength. This time, however, the USâ€“EU conflict also increases risk into February OpEx.Earnings seasonCorporate earnings in 2025 consistently beat expectations, and in early 2026 fundamentals, together with expected fiscal and monetary support, should continue to provide a stable backstop in the near term. In my piece titled The challenges of 2026, I laid out explicitly where bubble-like features are showing up in earnings reports (through Nvidia and TSMC).Wall Street expects 2025 Q4 to be the 10th consecutive quarter of positive year-on-year EPS growth for the index. The FactSet consensus is looking for around +8.2% EPS growth in Q4 (y/y). It is important to emphasize that the market entered earnings season with cautious expectations. Into year-end 2025, profit forecasts were restrained, partly due to tariff-war uncertainty and tough base effects. As a result, the bar is low, and early reporters have already cleared it: so far roughly 79% of S&P companies have beaten EPS consensus (slightly above the 5- and 10-year averages), although the magnitude of the beats is smaller than usual (about 5.8% versus a typical 7â€“8%), which can be interpreted as an early sign of tightening financing conditions.Over recent weeks, analyst estimates have edged up in some sectors (for example, consumer discretionary) and been revised down in others (energy, healthcare). Overall there has been no major negative surprise; a profit recession looks avoidable in the near term, and the market appears prepared for this outcome and is not treating it as an immediate bubble-burst signal.That said, profit growth has accelerated in cyclical sectors (industrials, materials, utilities, financials), while mega-cap tech is already comping a high base and is finding incremental growth harder. In parallel, profit declines are likely in four sectors (for example, consumer staples and energy) versus last year, driven by high bases (oil-sector windfall profits in 2022â€“23) and margin pressure.It is also important that profit growth is improving in sectors more directly tied to the real economy, and this is not yet reflected in index weights: indices remain heavily concentrated in a few mega-cap tech names. Improving results in the periphery can therefore create larger relative moves. For example, if an industrial conglomerate reports unexpectedly strong numbers, the stock can deliver meaningful relative outperformance even if it has limited impact on the index because its weight is small. In other words, the largest moves may come from sectors with small index weight but improving profit trends, which would further reinforce rotation. Final thoughtsThe Trump administration has placed excessive emphasis on equity indices as a headline indicator of success, with a weaker dollar also contributing meaningfully to returns. If the market were to correct 10â€“15% during 2026, Trumpâ€™s political capital could evaporate quickly; todayâ€™s tailwind of rising 401(k) balances could easily become a political vulnerability. Maintaining the equity boom through the midterms therefore becomes a key objective at almost any price. The real risk is that these trends are artificially sustained for too long, making any eventual correction even more painful, and ultimately crystallising longer-term credit non-payment risk as investments fail to earn an adequate return.In the short run, the machine still works: fiscal stimulus and the prospect of monetary stimulus, together with buyback flows, all reduce tail risk and provide support to the market, while injecting additional liquidity into sectors to sustain growth for as long as possible. Problems begin when the toolkit is exhausted, and they run out of ammo.Into February OpEx, tail risk remains elevated because of the ongoing USâ€“EU conflict. I think there is a meaningful probability of managed sell-offs designed to damp volatility, similar to last February. That would imply slower position reductions and high-volume intraday buy-the-dip speculation, aimed at reducing instability while systemic tail risk is still present. At the same time, liquidity is being channelled into the structural pivot areas I have laid out in my weekly posts, preventing the broader structure from failing. It is not only the algorithms; the narrative and retail speculators are also, for now, working in Trumpâ€™s favour.I still view the accumulation of risk, both geopolitically and from a market-valuation perspective, as becoming truly visible into the second quarter (the late-spring to summer window). That remains my window-of-risk target.It is important not to forget that, as the charts also show, geopolitical realignment and the search for the right narrative are what are currently driving markets and economies. This will end in a crisis, followed by a tokenized, AI-driven new economy.We are standing at the threshold of a historic regime change. Market analysis[free] SPX, Gold, BTC - A quick overview of the recent momentum and sentimentNov 18, 202522ShareHere I explained my window of risk call that I updated as policy is erratic nowadays, while sentiment is overoptimistic and not pricing in any bad news. Window of Risk Pt. 2 - Flows update AlmaÂ·October 29, 2025Read full storyNow I want to quick review how it is going now for the SPX, gold and Bitcoinâ€¦ SubscribeI wonâ€™t cover my precise quantitative outputs here (in terms of levels, dynamics and sentiment) like I do behind the paywall, but I do cover the overall momentums as they currently lookâ€¦SPX As long as the market cannot build structure above the â€œupside pivotâ€ marked area, the tendency remains risky and cautious. I personally does not expect it to happen in the near term as you know, market has seriously shaken. Earler I warned my followers on Twitter saying that going against seasonality is a big source of liquidity.SPX is currently testing the November lows that is a significant pivot sentiment wise, and both the weekly and intraday positioning derived pivots are coincidencing with this zone. Very important to watch it through the week. The downside target is the marked quite wide range. Last weekly and this current weekly positioning both points into that range. A 10% decline below 6200 would be healthy but I see low chance to happen due to the current motivations behind policy to cover any weaknesses. I think, more volatility is coming after VIX expo. Providing a potential buy-the-dip opportunity for an EOY rebound on a december hawkish Fed cut.But I will be careful with any of this. Simply because my warning earlier.Gold As long as Gold is building structure below the upside area marked with a yellow line, the odds are shifting towards a temporal retest of the lows as people are locking profit from gold. I suspect stronger dollar and rangebounding gold in the near-term as the most likely scenario. Second likeliest scenario is a gold retesting the marked upside then going below the pivot, while dollar starts to strenghten, then gold reverses back up. This would be a more natural trend, also would cause the beta to retest down a bit making higher low before going more up.Anyway, I expect gold reaching 5k in the next year. This call is still intact, I donâ€™t see any reason to change it. I donâ€™t play speculating game on cryptos, I only make really long-term trades with them. That will be the actual pivotal pattern. (Similar for Ethereum with 3700/6900, 3200 and 2880/3000 areas)All-in-allFor now, market has shaken, and trust in this economy and admin became really fragile for multiple reasons: erratic policy, insufficient foregn policy with big leaders, USA inner conflicts (like SCOTUS), stagflation, shutdown, missing autumn datas, too much mechanical flows-driven aggressive market trends, blindfolded Fed, corruption, shifting world-order, AI bubble (with growing technical and supply-chain concerns, and heavily concentrated market), and looming debt crisis that the leaders are not seem to be willing to handle properly. # GDP Release - Weekly post (22-26/Dec) [FREE post]

> Sentiment breakdown, GDP, Positioning breakdown

**Date:** 2025-01-29T22:11:46.429Z
**Source:** https://stochvoltrader.substack.com/p/gdp-release-weekly-post-22-26dec

---

Market analysisGDP Release - Weekly post (22-26/Dec) [FREE post]Sentiment breakdown, GDP, Positioning breakdownDec 20, 2025274ShareOn Dec 24, market closes at 1PM ET, and will be closed on Dec 25Liquidity vacuumLast week, the retest of the gap is happened as expected, however, as you will see below, the market is not convinced that the gap was actuall filled with liquidity. On Thursday and Friday and market formed too more gaps after some higher volatility days, that makes the zone still fragile. The weekly POC also falls at 6810, just above the gap. The positioning shows that market is still concerned about this liquidity vacuum downward, and it expects that to persist.It read like the market wants either â€œgo upâ€ on being optimistic, above 6900 now, or go down and retest the past weeks lows and build a â€œbasisâ€ there, before going up.GDP releaseMarket expects more local liquidity upward than downward, but there will be a significant sentiment-check on Tuesday: GDPThis is effectively the first official â€œcleanâ€ read on Q3 (BEA is doing two estimates instead of the usual three). The updated estimate (standing in for a typical third estimate) is scheduled for Jan 22, 2026.The common calendar consensus reading right now clusters around 3.2%, but Fed GDPNow has been running above thatâ€”about 3.5% (as of Dec 16), implying modest upside risk versus consensus. The SPX/yields beta for pricing in inflation scare:This print will decide if market believes in room for more upside this week, or if it frontrunned itself. If the data is weak, the market sees more Fed easing ahead. If the data comes strong that will erase the concerns about the future easing cycle. And market needs that liquidity. It will eventually get that, no doubt about it, the only question is: when.With a lot of datas missing, the odds are high that prints will be manipulated into a supportive print.If the print is â€œpositive supply-side shockâ€-ish (GDP up/prices down), that is the risk-on scenario.If the print is â€œnegative demand-side shockâ€-ish (GDP down/prices down), that is also benign, however the initial reaction will be pessimistic. If the print is â€œpositive demand-side shockâ€-ish (GDP up/prices up), the initial reaction will also be pessimistic as market re-prices its Fed cut odds. But if data is not hot, it also can get a benign read on the short-run too.If the print is â€œnegative supply-side shockâ€-ish (GDP down/prices up),thatâ€™s the stagflationary print, and market will not be happy at all.Based on my modelling, the most likely outcome is between the first and third outcome: GDP modestly above consensus, with the inflation measures (GDP price index/PCE prices in the GDP report) in-line to slightly softer than expected. Skewed towards â€œin-lineâ€, that is still price increase. So, given that it will get a â€œdatas were not fully collectedâ€ foggy narrative, this can take some time to digest positively.SubscribeBelow, I cover what the positioning says and what are the key levels derived from the volatility structure. And I will explain, step-by-step the conclusionsâ€¦ WEEKLY POSITIONING BREAKDOWNWEEKLY POSTHere is the weekly positioning:Speed profile The net speed profile is flat-to-positive. Customers are selling vol into both direction, but slightly more RV is being sold to the upside. The centroid of the profile is at 6798.90,but in order to get a proper stabilisation SPX needs to get above 6915.75, with a magnet clustering around 6928.60To the downside, the pivot is at 6688.88, with the most supportive cluster at 6670.34With the RV profile, market leaves a bit more room for downside moves, but aims to swallow it if it happens, while to the upside, it is net stabilization.Letâ€™s see, what the forward vol positioning tells usâ€¦Positioning derivativesNet gamma is positve, locally too, meaning customers expect compressed daily moves overall. Net color is negative until Thursday, then flips to positive into Friday, meaning, they leave a little room for momentum into midweek, but expect the spot to stabilize into Friday. Local magnets will come into effect.Net zomma is positive until Thursday, meaning participants expect missvalued volatility to take advange of, as IV/RV relationship is expected to remain inverse, but it flips to negative onto Friday, increasing the IV/RV correlation.Net vega is positive, butNet veta is negative and steeply so, meaning after an initial low IV state, they expect vol to increase into Friday. Net vomma is positive over the week, meaning, any volatility move is expected to be capped into both ways. The more vol is being bid, the more MMs will sell, and vice versa. Ultima profile says there is significantly more vomma effect to vol down moves, but it shifts into Friday. Net vanna is positive and very strong this week. So market expects shorter spot/vol beta to normalize, with supportive vol decay and suppressive vol expansion. Letâ€™s try to put it together, what it tells usâ€¦First, I want to say that the profile is beautifully consistent. Let me explain step by step.Both gamma decay and vega decay are priced to be negative this week. This means both realized volatility and implied volatility are expected to increase over the week. However, the slope is different and this is consistent with the zomma exposure!IV expansion is expected to be concave with a firm support from the lower levels due to higher downside ultima exposure (more vomma to buyback if vol decreases, creating a path of the least resistance to the upside for vol), however veta decay weakens as time passes and upside ultima increases creating a growing concavity to the upside. The RV expansion is way more flat, because 1) long zomma counterbalances the decay, and 2) the short downside speed also creates heavy upside concavity for RV. By modelling this, RV is rather expected to net rangebound with a flat positive drift, than increase convexly. And into Friday the RV is expected to be dumped but with a higher low. If it plays out, this means, IV also will be slightly down on Friday. What does it mean for SPX spot?Well, the IV/spot relationship is expected to be inverse due the to very heavy long vanna exposure. This means, the long skew traders expect to hit downside levels on the implied vol increase (see the vol projected ranges below). The RV expectation adds a bit more shade howeverâ€¦The speed profile is net flat-to-positive, this means a net very weak negative correlation between spot and RV, so this means, the net drift of the spot is expected to be rather net down until Friday. However, this is only a net expectation and very flat, almost zero correlation. The story depends on, which side of the centroid the spot is trading at.Because downside speed is sold and upside speed is bought by MMs, this says, that the market expects a rangebound around the centroid with a net flat-to-negative drift until Friday. But this rangebound is expected to widen from day to day, until it stabilizes into Friday potentially above the centroid. But this path is conditional: if spot is above the centroid into Friday in average, then the vol crush is expected to stabilize the spot upward. If it trades below the centroid on a net basis into Friday, then the stabilization is expected to be downward. Now, given the low (almost zero) asymmetry of the profile, and the increased correlation of IV/RV along with long vanna on Friday, it hints that the former scenario is the primal bet, with a flat weekly close. Do not be married to it! Positioning can drastically change, macro can surprise. Use this only as a base idea what the market is expecting.The key idea is that the market primarly expects a slight positive drift in vol, and long skew trades to catch a bid on uncertainity over the week, then stabilize the sentiment into Friday. Vomma rangesThe ranges for SPX that I can derive from vomma selling expectations, are at6691.65 - 6737.50 to the downside, and6910.23 - 6946.04 to the upside.These are the zones that are expected to be produced by a vol increase and decrease where vomma steps in the hardest. You can see the asymmetric expectations to the downside caused by the ultima and vanna exposures.Also note, that the lower bound of the upside zone is just 5 pts under the upside pivot derived from the speed profile, where the market aready expects stabilization.While, the downside pivot is 3 pts below the lower bound of the dowside zone. Farther from the point where the market expects downside stabilization.So given this asymmetrical expectation for the vomma to kick in, it kinda hints me that market has a â€œhidden reversion expectationâ€ in the worst case too, if everything remains under control.Fixed strike skew is bid, especially on the tails by 66.69%However the whole smirk moved downwards by ~32.07% The bid comes from heavy selling of 22-delta puts and even more 22-delta calls relative to the tail contracts. This also projects me a sentiment where participants have no real fear, but they expect to capitalize on long skew and short vomma trades during the week. All in all, the market expects undervaluedvalued uncertainity potential for the next week, that is reinforced by a negative drift in spot until mid-week, then we can see some contructive flows, but sentiment will remain moderated, skewed towards pessimism.For the GDP, the market sentiment is â€œbad news is good newsâ€/â€good news is bad newsâ€. The sentiment flips based on how fast the data print can be turned into a bullish narrative on this week.For Monday, the risk appetite expected to be moderate but slightly positive. For Tuesday, the GDP release can cause some increased uncertainity first. This release will be effectively the first official clean read on Q3. Market needs some time to digest it. I expect a moderated net negative sentiment, lowering risk appetit, and market needs to revaluate the datas one the longer horizont. The â€œinflation scareâ€ vs. â€œgrowth scareâ€ narrative may take some time to kick in about the datas.For Wednesday, we can expect a dull day, with some swing position close ahead of the holiday. Risk appetite expected to remain moderate. For Friday, we can expect the weekly sentiment to be stabilized. A bit more hint for pessimism, but we will see how we arrive into Friday, as said above.The expected distribution looks like this:The described expectation is derived purely from the positioning ahead.Donâ€™t be married to it. # Intraday post 19/march (+Fed)

> ...quick macro

**Date:** 2025-01-29T22:11:46.429Z
**Source:** https://stochvoltrader.substack.com/p/intraday-post-19march-fed

---

Market analysisIntraday post 19/march (+Fed)...quick macroMar 19, 2025162ShareI canâ€™t stress this enoughâ€”whether in my daily chat (in my first messages) or in my postsâ€”that the U.S. is struggling with stagflation. Trump has set out to eradicate this stagflation from the economy, even if only on paper. Last year was about two things: 1) Trump winning the election, and 2) figuring out when the Fed would cut rates. Thatâ€™s why we saw the Julyâ€“August vol squeeze, to give some room for the Fed. As I emphasized, the cut was a â€œhawkish cut,â€ purely for populist reasons, andâ€”as anticipatedâ€”inflationary pressure continued to rise. I kept showing this on Twitter, shorted the market, and voilÃ , I was right againâ€¦Inflation did not moderate last year; in fact, it only grew. The economy needs room so that the U.S. can achieve sustained, long-term, stable growth. Thatâ€™s what you need to understand. This is why everything you see happening is happening: the negative wealth effect. Leverage flush. Wall Street is reporting huge losses (even the renowned Renaissance), while dealer desks (like Citadelâ€™s MM department) are booking profits. Theyâ€™ll cover their losses during tax-harvesting time.Now, listen,Over the past three years, the Fed has been allowing a set amount of its bond holdings to mature without reinvesting the proceeds. This â€œrunoffâ€ drains reserves from the banking systemâ€”a process the Fed has used to gradually tighten monetary policy. In 2019, a similar reduction led to strains in overnight funding markets, forcing the Fed to reverse course.Now, with the looming need for Congress to raise the debt ceiling, thereâ€™s a risk that Treasury actions (like drawing down its general account to conserve cash) will distort reserve levels. If the Treasuryâ€™s cash is rebuilt quickly once the debt ceiling is extended, it could cause a rapid exit of reserves from the system. To avoid a potential liquidity crunch in the overnight markets (the â€œaltimeterâ€ of the financial system), Fed officials are considering a tactical pause or slowdown in the balance-sheet runoff. This would help ensure that reserves arenâ€™t drained too quickly during a period when market signals might be misleading because of the interplay between the Fedâ€™s operations and debt ceiling dynamics. This pause wouldnâ€™t indicate a change in the Fedâ€™s overall goal of reducing its balance sheetâ€”it would simply delay the process until after the debt ceiling issues are resolved and Treasury cash balances stabilize.The SPX/long-term yields correlation has risen 62.3 basis points since last Monday and is currently trending at 54%. So this doesnâ€™t just mean that good news is good news; it also means no news is good news, because investors see a pause in the runoff as reducing the risk of an abrupt reserve drain. In the short term, thatâ€™s supportive. Remember, based on the faked CPI and other reports, inflationary pressure appears to have eased.Letâ€™s see what the market is telling usâ€¦ INTRADAYKeep my weekly post in mindâ€¦Strong futs overnight.The models show that since last Wednesday, the market has been oscillating intraday (just as I predicted it would) with a slight neutral-to-positive drift and relatively low variance. However, the ADF test still does not indicate any tendency toward a mean-reverting phase in the broader momentum. That said, the reversion model shows a 97.62% probability of reversion, but I want to emphasize again that, on a longer timeframe, the marketâ€™s momentum does not suggest a shift toward a mean-reverting phase. So this signal is more of a supportive signal rather than a strictly reversion one. Intraday, however, the oscillation is very strong. According to the model, as long as the SPX can hold the 5523.5 level, the positive drift remains intact.As I mentioned, funds are in mean reversion mode during RTH (regular trading hours). This means that whatever they do during the Asian and London sessions, they reverse during RTH, causing oscillations.Yesterday, however, the VIX options technically expired, and the beta hedging trades in ES put pressure on the index, as the VIX was pinned around 21.Letâ€™s take a look at the skew. Here, you can see todayâ€™s 5-delta put â€“ 5-delta call range: If we measure the skew slope for the 25d Put/ATM, 25d Call/ATM, and 25d Put/25d Call segments, we can observe that since yesterday, the slope has decreased slightly. However, compared to one week ago, there is a 3.51% increase in the longer skew. But if we look at the ATM vs. call and ATM vs put segments, we see that itâ€™s not demand for puts that has grown; rather, demand for calls has fallen.Compared to the values from February 24, the slope has decreased by 8.84%, which indicates a shorter skewâ€”and indeed, it stems from the put side.The VIX is quite similar enough.At the same time, weâ€™re seeing a moderate increase on the tail-put side (and on tail-calls as well!). Itâ€™s not huge, but we need to pay attention because it affects the vol profileâ€™s sensitivity. I code 5611.96 as our main pivot level, and 5523.77 (very close to the 5523.5 my momentum model highlightedâ€”no coincidence!) as the point below which the trend turns decisively more bearish. That level should be taken very seriously today.Thereâ€™s also something else: looking at the Friday AM expiration vol profile, the model gives 5622.03 as todayâ€™s pivot. 10 pts above the intraday vol profile based pivot. And weâ€™re currently almost at their geometric midpoint (3 points below it). Not by coincidence. Itâ€™s a typical footprint of heavy algo trading.From the vol profileâ€™s perspective, 5567.27 is another crucial level for the bullsâ€”if puts donâ€™t catch a bid there, the trend wonâ€™t start rolling downhill. If they stay calm in that zone, put decay will be supportive.For upward momentum, 5698.85 is the key level per the vol profileâ€”itâ€™s a trend-reversal threshold. But watch 5656.83 carefully, to see if calls catch a bid. That will be your signal of how strong the upside could be.OptionsDepth chart: (Description is here)Coding zero vanna at 5608 (high vol needed for break through).From positioning perspective the move can be stabilizied by MM flow above 5711We have a MM long fly patter with 5600 in the middle. Short speed below, long speed above.In theory, we should see increased spot/vol beta below 5535.52, and decreased spot vol beta above 5659.26, and â€˜feelâ€™ the longer gamma effect.This setup favors for vol increase in theory and wider rangebound. Below 5613 the charm flows turn positive (putting dealers in longer delta in every 5 mins, forcing them to sell futs).Color (charm convexity) is negative, meaning, the gamma decay is on, during the session, and this favors for more volatility. # Intraday post (28/feb)

> Coded gamma for today expo:

**Date:** 2025-01-29T22:11:46.429Z
**Source:** https://stochvoltrader.substack.com/p/intraday-post-28feb

---

Market analysisIntraday post (28/feb)Feb 28, 20252722ShareCoded gamma for today expo:3D chart, my heatmap. OptionsDepth:Stochastic Volatility - Options market insights is a reader-supported publication. To receive new posts and support my work, consider becoming a free or paid subscriber.Subscribe Coding zero vanna at 5914 (positive vanna convexity, vol has to calm down to break above this line), and downside vanna flip at 5795.65, here you should see vol up to break through this line (negative vanna convexity).Significant flip points from gamma perspective for intraday trading at 5890 and 5856As you can see on the chart, locally we are in a negative speed environment that is mechanically suppressive (as char nor a vol crush arenâ€™t supportive), but still accelerant to the upside towards the vanna flip with increase spot/vol beta, short-term gamma squeeze. I code 5854.77 as the pivot for that.We also have negative charm convexity = short color, meaning these low gammas will furter decrease into PM, making the profile more steep, adding to vol and suppressive flows into EoD. MMs have deltas to buyback, we will likely see that in the opening, but as time passes, long charm exposure will increase put deltas and MMs will sell, if spot cannot grind above 5934.48 before PMFrom mean reversion perspective, SPX is likely to forming a near-term bottom again: But as long as I donâ€™t see another new white dot, Iâ€™m not convinced about the strenght of the move more than a bounce. Code says, SPX should hold above 5953.38 to confirm upward momentum. â€œSpot decayâ€I spent some time explaining in the chat this week since Sunday, my call about a hedged spot decay, where downside vol cannot really catch up in avg, and the market slowly grinding lower into a supportive March OpEx. I explained this call in the Tuesday morning post, with link to the chat explaination. I already saw this kind of pattern in â€˜22 and also in â€˜23 too. What this means is that While the net trend points down, there is not enough intraday edge on the puts side bcs the trade is crowded. However the call side edge is better bcs of the underpriced odds. Personally while I still hold my puts I bought at 19th Wednesday close into March expo, I look for intraday call edge reversion trades and not building directional exposure until Q1. The expo will be covered on Sunday post. VIX call accumulationWe can see accumulation of VIX call spreads on both April and May expos.Now, you better know, that in itself it is not very telling, bcs it can be a simply rebalancing activity from some large portfolio. We could see similar like back in jan 17 last year. What we must do in this situation is to watch for sudden spikes in the prices of near-term VIX calls and SPX far tail puts (e.g. 5-10 deltas), like 1-week or 1-month calls, and also watch the trend if the VIX momentum is sticky at higher sigma lvls or not (my shared SD indicator can help with this), in order to catch actually tail-risk expectations. Here you can see the multi-expiry skew for both SPX and VIX into next week, March expo, April and May: Now, in itself these arenâ€™t quite telling. What we have to look for is the CHANGE in the pricing of these events like from post-NVDA ER, and 1 week ago vs current: What we see here is rather a slow kind of grind up in SPX tail puts, but we can see the spike in tail calls into next Friday. Lets look at VIX into March 17 Vix expo: Now, here we see some significant increase during the week in the 42C and 60C IVs (like ~30 bps), not as much as what we would expect, but its there. Note, that we donâ€™t see this kind of change into April or May VIX expos: This tells me more lika a â€˜sticky high VIXâ€™ environment that is hedges due to , than fear of left-tail event. Similar with SPX, into March OpEx, 5-10 delta puts at 5450 - 5220 are rather decreased relative to post-NVDA ER than increased, while right wing is bid: Same with April and May: So, these higher order activities are rather noise for now than actual left-tail concerns. This, along with my reversion signals puts me like more the call side than the put side. Mean reversionThe probability for a mean reversion up is pretty much elevated. Both of my models now give green signals, the more sensitive one too: Model says that for the short-term upward momentum, spot needs to conquer 5953.38For the longer-term, the lvl is 6119.32 Note, that this is a negative skewed probability distirbution. And this tells higher probability for up than down from here, temporary. Negative event have lower probability, but higher impact.I hedge the left-tail, while going for intraday call edge. # Iran-risk and oil prices

> Timing is lost

**Date:** 2025-01-29T22:11:46.429Z
**Source:** https://stochvoltrader.substack.com/p/iran-risk-and-oil-prices

---

Free Insights | Market ReportsIran-risk and oil pricesTiming is lostFeb 24, 2026242ShareTiming is lost Regarding military intervention in Iran, Trump has missed the window of opportunity. Both British and Arab intelligence agencies are unanimously attempting to dissuade him from any kind of military operation, particularly during Ramadan (a window lasting approximately until the March OpEx), as such an action would directly ignite a jihad in the region and lead to an Arab Spring 2.0.Such an operation would precipitate a localized humanitarian disaster, massively drive up oil prices (especially since Arab oil refineries and shadow fleets would also sustain damage), and further exacerbate supply chain disruptions, all of which would collectively deepen Western stagflation.This, in turn, would provide China with an opportunity to enforce a blockade along the First Island Chain, exerting further pressure on Trump (which would bolster the Democratsâ€™ position domestically). The crack spread (long gasoil/short Brent) shows bid on March and May contract:The spread is above its 95th percentile since November correction, signaling steep backwardation.And this comes from gasoil, that means refinery margin, distillate premium.Meanwhile, in contrast to this, the Brent front-month versus 6-month spread has been trending lower since June last year. This is a serious divergenceâ€¦On the one hand, this signals the risk of supply disruptions; on the other hand, it indicates that the regime continues to adapt.Brent shows massive call demand for May 26 expiry:So does gasoil:The geopolitical and global economic risks of this would be immense, as it would drastically degrade the negotiating leverage of the United States on a global scale. SubscribeThe risk of any military operationLet me outline how the assessment of such a strike is conducted. The success of the intervention hinges on whether the Washington-backed son of the Shah is capable of forging the opposition into a unified front and sufficiently undermining the Ayatollahâ€™s grip on power. However, intelligence agencies cannot gather exact data on this; they can only rely on probabilities. This was also the case in 1979, when U.S. intelligence deceived itself by seeing only what it wanted to see in the data. The U.S. military is unequivocally robust enough to execute the operation, but the focal point of the assessment is whether it would actually yield the expected results or merely further destabilize the environment. Unfortunately, Trump waited too long here; the regime has adapted, closed ranks even more tightly after the initial tremors, and prepared for American intervention. So timing is lost. Iran is buying time through negotiation to get fully prepared after RamadanTo comprehend Middle Eastern conflicts, one must understand that their roots are fundamentally ideological, rather than diplomatic or economic. The latter are merely secondary, sometimes entirely fabricated pretexts. Factions are held together precisely by these ideologies; if an individual emerges who can take the helm and authentically represent the most widely accepted ideology, they can forge the group into a cohesive bloc. Therefore, the critical question intelligence agencies must currently evaluate is whether the oppositionâ€™s faith in Persian culture and the unifying authority of the Shah are at least as strong as the fear of the Islamic religion and the believersâ€™ loyalty to their group. (This is especially pertinent given that the plunge of the rial is due to an artificial dollar shortage engineered by the U.S. In such scenarios, autocratic regimes typically adopt a victimhood posture.) Without this ideological counterbalance, the regime cannot be overthrown, and a Venezuela-style operation would only result in a power vacuum and civil war.It is crucial to understand that the driving force behind the idea of an American intervention is Israel, which seeks to guarantee its own security through the preemptive dismantling of Iranâ€™s nuclear and ballistic missile programs. However, because the roots of power are inherently ideological, regime change is essential for long-term success. An American strike would undoubtedly cause destabilization, but it could subsequently foster stronger cohesion within the system. This probability is remarkably high, as this is exactly what is currently observable. The loyalty of the security forces remains steadfast; moreover, they have proven their allegiance to the regime. Preparations for succession are proceeding without conflict, there is no internal strife within the regime stemming from the crisis, official communication is disciplined and consistent (showing no signs of panic or disarray), and the repressive apparatus shows no signs of fatigue, continuing to employ lethal force and internet blackouts. Furthermore, the opposition demographic driving the intent for regime change is highly fragmented. Acceptance of the Shahâ€™s son is by no means unanimous, either among the diaspora or Iranians living at home, and the protest coalition is heavily fractured and episodic, failing to genuinely aggregate into a unified bloc. Finally, Iran is actively preparing for an American military operation (efforts include dispersing leadership and command-and-control centers over a broader area, maintaining heightened readiness in the Strait of Hormuz, burying tunnels in Isfahan, reinforcing the Pickaxe Mountain entrances near Natanz, and implementing â€œconcrete sarcophagusâ€-style coverings at Parchin, among other measures). As long as the aforementioned factors do not exhibit structural cracks, any form of external intervention will prove futile. The initial conditions were favorable, but Trump waited too long. Gold futures:Gold futures 3-months, 6-months, 1-year agoShareStochastic Volatility Trader - Quant Insights is a reader-supported publication. # OpEx, Intraday post (20/march) + Fed path and tech (with geos)

> Crucial post

**Date:** 2025-01-29T22:11:46.429Z
**Source:** https://stochvoltrader.substack.com/p/opex-intraday-post-20march-fed-path

---

Market analysisOpEx, Intraday post (20/march) + Fed path and tech (with geos)Crucial postMar 20, 20251814ShareFOMC officials highlighted increased uncertainty and a tilt toward stagflation. Growth forecasts were marked down to about 1.7% for this year, while inflation projections were revised upward for 2025. Earlier, policymakers anticipated a â€œsoft landingâ€ in 2025, gradually lowering interest rates while controlling inflation and maintaining low unemployment. Now, the projections indicate that tariffs are likely to push prices higher, slow economic growth, and increase unemployment, making rate cuts less feasible in the near term.Inflationary pressures stemming from tariffs are proving more persistent than initially anticipated. Powell emphasized that the latest inflation uptick is being driven by an external, tariff-related source.They also announced a significant slowdown in quantitative tightening, from $25 billion to $5 billion per month, which supports a further decline in short-end yields and contributes to front-end spread widening. In response, U.S. rates fell, the yield curve steepened on downside risks, and the USD depreciated slightly.Powellâ€™s press conference was considered more dovish than the SEP implied, with Powell dismissing some longer-term inflation expectations as outliers.The SEP from the FOMC showed a heavy skew toward weaker economic activity and higher inflation risks. While median projections call for two 25bp cuts in 2025 and 2026, the dot plotâ€™s distribution indicates substantial uncertainty, with many participants anticipating fewer cuts. This raises concerns that the Fed could be caught flat-footed if â€œtransitoryâ€ inflation pressures persist.Former Fed officials suggest that if tariff-induced price hikes become entrenched, the Fed may be forced to rethink its policy approach, potentially delaying or even foregoing further rate cuts.The key point I want to emphasize is that the Fedâ€™s dovish rhetoric is underestimating persistent inflation/stagflation risks. As I keep stressing, the negative wealth effect cycle is not over. However the market needs liquidity for further moves now.For now, we can now see that the equity vs. long-term yields correlation remains highly positive. This is a direct result of bull steepening, driven by concerns about U.S. economic growth and expectations that any downturn is already priced in. Investors are anticipating further easing (keeping short-term rates low), while long-term yields remain anchored by longer-term growth and inflation expectations, hence the positive correlation.Meanwhile, newspapers are starting to report that sovereign Middle Eastern funds are showing increased interest in U.S. tech stocks, and the U.S.â€“Russia gas extraction deal is also taking shape.Ceasefire negotiations are also moving forward slowly, in a positive direction - as much as Iâ€™m allowed to tell you.My post about geos is very important. This is what dictates the market as well. This is what is happening. INTRADAY POSTCoding gamma for Friday AM expo:The speed profile is net negative to neutral, with a tail-to-tail slope of -0.13%, but only -0.08% from the midpoint toward tail calls and tail puts.Iâ€™m coding 5595 as the level where puts should start to catch a bid in theory for significant downward strenght, and from there we should start to feel the longer downside gamma effect on the intraday vol profile. Also coding 5680.43 as the level where calls should catch a bid; however, itâ€™s a shorter upside gamma effect, but I donâ€™t think it will significantly affect the intraday vol profile, since the speed exposure isnâ€™t steep enough.The main daily pivot is 5623.59, mark it.The charm profile is net suppressive-to-neutral here, favoring a pinning at the daily pivot. Locally, we also have a very mild positive color (charm convexity) that encourages intraday volatility to be compressed as gamma increases by the time. But remember, lower volatility leads to longer MM delta exposure. At the same time, lower volatility reduces the vanna effect, so theoretically, this setup favors for an oscillating, slightly suppressive trend.As I always say, any deviation will reveal the hands of the hidden customer flow. This is how we use the dealer profile.The models show me that on a wider timeframe any meanâ€‘reverting behavior in the price levels is even weaker now. While on an intraday basis it sees very strong meanâ€‘reversion in the shortâ€‘term fluctuations. So while the overall price level wanders (nonâ€‘stationarity per ADF), the intraday fluctuations are corrected rapidly. The overall regime remains stable, oscillating with a slight positive-to-zero drift.Letâ€™s look at tech alphaâ€¦Here you can see the 20-day rolling tech alpha relative to the SPX benchmark. Below it are the ROC (Rate of Change) values of the alpha curve, as well as their weekly average.We can see that the trend is similar to the behavior we observed last Octoberâ€“November. NVDA still hasnâ€™t caught a bid, nor have AAPL, GOOG, or TSLA. MSFT, META, and AMD are leading the dance instead. For the trend to continue, itâ€™s crucial that their â€œfriendsâ€ catch up soon. The reason is that NVDA and AAPL are heavily exposed to China, while the U.S. aims to strengthen its own manufacturing and reduce reliance on Chinaâ€”a country they ultimately want to push out of economic processes once the new â€œHoly Allianceâ€ is in place.The U.S. is adopting export controls, investment bans, and significant domestic R&D funding to limit Chinaâ€™s access to cutting-edge technologies like advanced AI chips and quantum computing. Meanwhile, China is investing billions in indigenous innovation to reduce dependence on Western technology, fueling a high-stakes investment race.Quantum computing is emerging as a crucial frontier, with contributions from major tech giants (IBM, Google, Microsoft, Amazon) as well as pure-play startups (IonQ, Rigetti, etc.) and government-funded initiatives. Thereâ€™s growing interest from Wall Streetâ€”seen in SPAC deals and large VC investmentsâ€”to support companies that may eventually offer a strategic advantage. At the same time, geopolitical concerns are driving Western efforts to limit Chinese involvement in this sensitive area.Saudi Arabiaâ€™s Public Investment Fund (PIF), led by MBS, is aggressively channeling vast capital into tech sectors (AI, semiconductors, quantum computing) by backing vehicles like SoftBankâ€™s Vision Fund and making direct investments (e.g., in EVs and chip technologies). Other Gulf funds, such as Mubadala and ADIA, are also stepping upâ€”often partnering with Israeli and Western investors. Strengthened by the Abraham Accords, these growing ties create a network where Middle Eastern capital now fuels innovation in regional hubs like Tel Aviv as well as in global tech centers. # OpEx, VIXpery and PCE week | Weekly post (17-20/Feb) 

> Python quant course is already available on my Substack-site, by an ex-Wall Street quant.

**Date:** 2025-01-29T22:11:46.429Z
**Source:** https://stochvoltrader.substack.com/p/opex-vixpery-and-pce-week-weekly
